            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Vargas has prodigious power, and if you cross your eyes, he's almost a dead ringer for David Ortiz. Well, a switch-hitting version who doesn't walk. But that's enough for Twins fans, who no doubt have sky-high expectations for the Puerto Rican slugger after not only seeing him double in the Future's Game at Target Field, but come up for a 53-game cup of coffee that saw him poke 20 extra-base hits and slug .456. Unfortunately, that doesn't account for the part of his game that may be his undoing. Vargas' plate discipline was borderline ghastly, as he had a 63-10 strikeout-to-unintentional-walk ratio in his first 234 big league plate appearances. The belief in national prospect circles was that Vargas wasn't a good defensive first baseman -- this much is true -- and this his power wouldn't be propped up by enough contact or pitch recognition skills to truly shine through. The Twins have seen hot stints in short bursts from pretty good prospects before. Chris Parmelee and Josmil Pinto's Septembers the past few seasons come to mind. But Vargas is going to get the first crack at regular DH at bats at the beginning of the season, and he has the kind of power to truly take your breath away. The odds are probably still against him, but the opportunity is there for the taking. I probably wouldn't draft him, but that doesn't mean he can't be successful. (Brandon Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Vargas' pitch recognition and contact skills will always be in question, but if he can get them going, his power will make him a truly special player. As a utility-only bat in most leagues, he's a good power threat but likely won't walk much or have a passable batting average. Roster construction will determine just how highly you should value him.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The sun has most likely set on Vargas' time as a big leaguer, at least in a Twins uniform. Not only did the organization bury him in 2015 -- sending him all the way to Double-A after a slow start -- but they went out and acquired Korean designated hitter Byung Ho Park as well as promoting Miguel Sano over the last year. Add to that the already crowded scene with Joe Mauer at first base, and Vargas would need a change of scenery to see significant time in the major leagues. The knock on Vargas the hitter was that he had holes in his swing and would sometimes expand the strike zone, and his .240/.277/.349 batting line and 29.3% whiff rate in 184 big league plate appearances last year fits that bill. He can hit the ball a country mile and bears a strong resemblance to David Ortiz physically, but that couldn't be further from the truth skills-wise, at least in present-day form. (Brandon Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Vargas' solid debut in 2014 gave way to a disappointing 2015, and he's likely to spend all of 2016 in the minors barring an injury in front of him. He could be a cheap source of power if called up, but there are caveats. Tread lightly.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After flailing through a wholly disappointing 2015 season, Vargas became a three-true-outcome dynamo in 2016. Vargas' work with hitting coach Chad Allen down at Triple-A helped rework his plate approach, and while the results weren't overwhelmingly positive with Rochester, he did manage to bump his walk rate  something that transferred when the Twins called him up. Vargas got 177 plate appearances with the Twins in 2016, with 51.4% resulting in a walk, a strikeout or a home run. Vargas hit a respectable .230/.333/.500 in those plate appearances, though the splits were a bit... strange. Vargas, a switch-hitter, batted a remarkable .378/.462/.800 against left-handed pitching but just .168/.280/.374 against righties. It's probably just a strange aberration in those small sample sizes, but it's still a bit interesting, nonetheless. At the very least, Vargas  whom the Twins petitioned for and received a fourth option year on  should get another reasonable chance as the team's DH moving forward. There's sleeper potential for 25-30 home runs here. (@Brandon_Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Keep an eye on Vargas. If he's given the full-time DH job, there's potential for significant power and even some walks in saber-friendly leagues. He still has to fend off Byung-ho Park and any bat the Twins may sign this offseason for full-time work, however.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>

<script>var customNoShow = false;</script><script>var dataPlayerCaps=[{"season": "2015",
            "profile": "Vargas has prodigious power, and if you cross your eyes, he's almost a dead ringer for David Ortiz. Well, a switch-hitting version who doesn't walk. The belief in national prospect circles was that Vargas wasn't a good defensive first baseman -- this much is true -- and this his power wouldn't be propped up by enough contact or pitch recognition skills to truly shine through. The Twins have seen hot stints in short bursts from pretty good prospects before. Chris Parmelee and Josmil Pinto's Septembers the past few seasons come to mind. But Vargas is going to get the first crack at regular DH at bats at the beginning of the season, and he has the kind of power to truly take your breath away. The odds are probably still against him, but the opportunity is there for the taking. I probably wouldn't draft him, but that doesn't mean he can't be successful. (Brandon Warne)",

Add to that the already crowded scene with Joe Mauer at first base, and Vargas would need a change of scenery to see significant time in the major leagues. The knock on Vargas the hitter was that he had holes in his swing and would sometimes expand the strike zone, and his .240/.277/.349 batting line and 29.3% whiff rate in 184 big league plate appearances last year fits that bill. He can hit the ball a country mile and bears a strong resemblance to David Ortiz physically, but that couldn't be further from the truth skills-wise, at least in present-day form. Vargas got 177 plate appearances with the Twins in 2016, with 51.4% resulting in a walk, a strikeout or a home run. Vargas hit a respectable .230/.333/.500 in those plate appearances, though the splits were a bit... strange. Vargas, a switch-hitter, batted a remarkable .378/.462/.800 against left-handed pitching but just .168/.280/.374 against righties. It's probably just a strange aberration in those small sample sizes, but it's still a bit interesting, nonetheless.     function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setPart(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi' || node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

<script type="text/javascript">
    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
</script>
